text:
My aunt has been making this recipe for years & has given me a few pointers....as Hollyfae said, be sure & make sure your cream cheese is all the way to the edges of the pan & sealed (to keep the jello from seeping under the cream cheese & making the crust soggy). It's also helpful to chill the cream cheese really well before topping w/ the jello.  Sometimes I like to add an 8 oz. can of crushed pineapple in w/ the strawberries (Paula Deen's version)

text:
A hit every time I make it!  Do not try to substitute low fat cream cheese or cool whip... the white layer just won't come together as nicely.  I learned the hard way.  Multiple times.  Make sure to spread the white layer all the way to the edges and get a nice seal so that the jello layer doesn't seep into the bottom.  In the spring and early summer, when strawberries are in season around here, I also slice some fresh berries into the jello for presentation.

I love this recipe but found it much better if after the jello is all disolved I add 4 ice cubes until melted then add an 8 oz tub of whipped cream to the jello mixture and mix til smooth then adding the strawberries after. It stays more firm and has a wonderful creamy taste to it.

text:
SOME TIPS:  This is an easy recipe to follow, but I can understand why people are having a problem with the layers.  Thru my experience, this is what I did and didnt seem to have a problem with any of the layers seeping thru.  FIRST-COOL THE CRUST COMPLETELY!!  SECOND-CREAM THE SUGAR AND CREAM CHEESE THOROUGHLY!  SPREAD ON PRETZEL MIXTURE AND REFRIGERATE AT LEAST 30-45 MINUTES.  PREPARE JELLO AS DIRECTED BY DISSOLVING COMPLETELY FOR TWO MINUTES  AND ADD FROZEN, SLICED STRAWBERRIES.  LET SIT FOR ABOUT 5 MINUTES STIRRING FREQUENTLY DURING THOSE FIVE MINUTES UNTIL IT IS LIKE A JELLIED, SOFT TEXTURE.  I USED A METAL WHISK TO ACCOMPLISH THIS. POUR OVER REFRIGERATED CREAM CHEESE LAYER.  REFRIGERATE UNTIL SET, ABOUT A COUPLE OF HOURS.  HOPE THIS HELPS!!!!

text:
This was really fun to make. I only added just a little vanilla to the cream cheese/whipped topping layer. Other than that, I made no changes. I did follow other reviewer's suggestions and chill the layers in-between layering. Made for an easier time of layering. I also made sure to go right to the edges with the cream cheese layer to keep from the jello layer from seeping through and making the "crust" soggy. Fun! EDITED NEXT DAY: I LOVED the top and bottom layers. They were wonderful together. The bottom layer was.....just not right for this dessert. If I were to make this again, I'd double a recipe for graham cracker crust and use that instead of the pretzels. It just wasn't good. EDITED AGAIN A WEEK LATER: I made this again today with a crust made from Lorna Doone cookies. I just followed the same recipe, only using two sleeves of crushed Lorna Doone cookies. Much better.
EDITED YET AGAIN: I made the top layer today with Blackberry Fusion Jello and this summer's blackberries. Fabulous. Not as overpoweringly sweet as the strawberries.

It is a great potluck recipe.

I've been making this recipe for years, but I make a few modifications that make it even better.  First, instead of strawberry jello and berries, I use raspberry jello and frozen raspberries.  The day before, I let the berries thaw over a collander.  Once I have collected that juice, I combine it with boiling water to make the 2 cups the recipe calls for.  Makes the top layer much more interesting.

Delicious!  I followed the recipe exactly, except lessening the water added to the jello a little bit due to juices in some of my frozen strawberries.  I cooked the crust just 8 minutes to avoid having a too hard crust.  Also, I chilled the cream cheese layer for a half hour or so before adding the jello.  I recommend letting the jello firm up a little while in the fridge before pouring it over the cream cheese layer if you are having a mixing problem.  This was great!

text:
This is a wonderful recipe!  I make it slightly different than the recipe though.  Instead of using a 9x13 pan, I use a bundt pan and make the recipe in the opposite order (jello part first, then the cream layer, and the pretzels last).  Of course, I am not able to toast the pretzel part, but it still turns out really well.  Spray the bundt pan with non-cook cooking spray before starting and then turn over onto a plate once it is done setting.  It looks as great as it tastes!

text:
After reading numerous reviews, I made this, and it turned out "Perfect"! Everyone is saying that the crust gets 'soggy', I have made this 5 times and it has never gotten soggy, even after it has been in the fridge for several days. I made it exactly like the recipe says except for this: I am a diabetic, so I used sugar-free jello, and I used Splenda instead of sugar. If it is made correctly, the crust will not get soggy. It is not the recipe that causes the soggy crust; it is the preparer. A wonderful recipe!!

text:
The first time I made this, I cut a lot of corners calorie-wise by using fat-free cream cheese (I figured it'd be okay since the crust was the only thing being baked), fat-free cool whip and sugar-free jello, and half splenda.  Man, do not do this.   Usually I'm not picky with those things, but this is one of those recipes that you think you can do that with because it doesn't involve a lot of baking, and it just does not work. The second time was much better. I used brown sugar on the crust and it was a little less chewy and a little more savory. Oh, and I would definitely recommend letting the jello set up a little before pouring it over everything else. If your strawberries are frozen, the jello will set quickly. I used fresh strawberries once and couldn't for the life of me get the jello to set, but then added a few ice cubes and that took care of it.

All time favorite of my family for holidays! Tips for crushing pretzels, put in ziplock bag and use rolling pin to crush as fine as you prefer. Make sure to pull the cream cheese/cool whip mixture to the edge of the pan or jello mixture will seep onto crust. Let jello/strawberries mixture stiffen up while you make crust, however don't let set entirely or will not smooth over cheese nicely.  Enjoy!

text:
Yum! I love this recipe. Thanks so much for sharing. I have made this dish for several years now, and your version of the recipe is very nice. Since I am usually serving a crowd, I used my 10 x 15 x 2 clear glass pan. I used your recipe with one extra block of cream cheese as I like a thick layer and had a bigger pan. I couldn't find 2 (10 oz) pkgs of frozen strawberries, so I used one 16 oz bag. I also like my strawberries not so whole, so I used a potato masher on them. For the crust I cooked it for 8 minutes this time, but it was sort of fragile. I have cooked it longer and it has gotten too hard... So for my oven I think 10 minutes is perfect. VERY IMPORTANT: Spread cream cheese all the way to the edges of the pan to keep the strawberries from seeping into the crust and making it soggy. Also, you must chill the strawberry mixture before you put it on the cream cheese layer, or it will melt its way through. I also chill the cream cheese layer while I am freezing the strawberry mixture until it is thickened. I am also very careful when adding the strawberry layer... I spoon the strawberries on and then slowly/carefully pour the rest of the juice. You must leave plenty of time for this to chill as it needs time to harden. I always make this the day before.

text:
Being philosophically opposed to Cool Whip, I made my own whipped cream in a stand mixer with 8 oz. of heavy cream. I used 20 oz. fresh strawberries which I washed, sliced and froze on a piece of wax paper on a plate. Pretzels went into my food processor in two batches, approximately 7 oz. total thin pretzels. Crust was magnificent, baked 10 minutes. I allowed it to cool completely, no rushing.  Cream cheese layer kept the jello away from the crust exactly as advised after spreading it to the edges of the glass pan. I chilled the second layer before adding the jello. It is a delectable, attractive layered dessert, cuts easily when cold. New favorite thing!

text:
I love pretzel jello.  This was something my mom made every holiday and has lots of fond memories attached to it.  With this particular recipe there are just a couple problems.  First there isn't enough pretzel crust.  You need 3 cups of pretzels so that the crust isn't too thin and hits all the spots.  When you add the extra cup of pretzels don't increase the butter.  There was too much.  And as for the delicious white, middle layer.  Yummy!  But there is far too much!  If I had put it all in the pan there would have been no room to pour the jello on top.  So cut the recipe for the white stuff in half.  The awesome thing about this recipe is you can do it up anyway you like.  Try lemon jello and raspberries.  Super pretty!

read reviews about mushy pretzels.

I've been making this for years. It has become my requested dish for extended family gatherings. I have added a third box of jello without increasing the liquid to help the jello set. My hint for spreading the white layer is to use 2 spoons to spread & a lot of patience! Also,once the crust is baked, you can transfer it to smaller containers or nonbakeware to finish jello. The smaller containers help it last longer, as it only gets soggy after initial serving.

text:
I make this for parties in the spring and summer.  It's a GREAT recipe and there's never any leftovers!  The last time I made it, however, I did learn a valuable lesson.  Do not use cream cheese that's been in the freezer and defrosted.  If I buy cream cheese on sale, I'll usually toss it in the freezer.  It's ok in something that you bake (cheesecakes, etc.) but NOT good in something that is meant to set up in the refrigerator.  The middle layer remained too runny and never really set up well.  It still tasted great, but I knew it wasn't perfect!

text:
This turned out perfectly!  I crushed up one 8 oz bag of mini pretzels and made certain the crust was completely cooled; even chilled in the refrigerator for 15 minutes.  After making the whipped topping, I also put it in the refrigerator for 20 minutes.  Just need to make certain the crust is COMPLETELY COOLED and the whipped topping is THICK & CHILLED.  Like other reviews, I made certain to spread the whipped topping to the edges and in the corners.  I wiped down the pan to clean up any stray whipped topping.  For the jello topping, I boiled 2 cups of water and poured in the jello packets, stirring for about 2 min.  I then turned off the heat & added the sliced frozen strawberries.  I took my salad chopper to crush up some of the strawberries, then stirred, let it sit for 5 minutes, stirring a couple of times.  It was pretty thick and ready to spread on top.  Looks picture perfect!!!

text:
Alright yall. I was a little confused if I had to make the jello like the actual BOX or just the boiling 2 cups of water and add strawberries. SO glad I listened to my gut and just did the 2 cups boiling water and then mixed the strawberries in. PHEW! Like all the reviews say, Make sure that crust is COOLED! Also make sure you spread the cream cheese mixture with no holes in it and seal it so no pretzels are showing and nothing can seep into it. Then chill the pretzels and cream cheese in the fridge for 45-60 mins. Then pour the jellowed strawberries over it! Refrigerate for a couple of hours. I made mine the day before I needed it and all was well.  NOMZ! Thanksgiving and Christmas tradition!!

I always loved this Salad but hadn't made it in years.  I read all of the helpful ideas from previous reviews and added my own.  I made sure that the whipped cream and cream cheese was cold before putting on top of the pretzels.  Making sure to go all the way to the edges to not allow the jello mix to seep into the pretzels.  Also the jello and strawberry mix I let is sit for about an hour before adding to the top making sure that I stirred the mixture to blend the strawberries into the jello.  Other than that easy and simple recipe.

country:
None
text:
This is the first jello salad I have ever made.  It turned out perfectly.  I took it to Christmas and everyone raved about it.   

I read many reviews and do not understand how anyone could "flop" this and not have it turn out.  

Never use generic or low fat CoolWhip (you will not have a good outcome if you do).  Do not use low fat cream cheese. 

The pretzel crust is the perfect blend of salt/sweet and complements the jello/strawberries perfectly.  I would not change this pretzel crust to a graham crust.  

When spreading the cream cheese layer, like others suggested, make sure to spread this layer all the way to the edges, so the jello layer doesn't seep through to the crust and get it soggy.  

Good luck keeping this for leftovers, everyone will want a second helping.

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/7400601.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Very good! Easy to make. 

1. You can use a food processor for the pretzels, pulse until they are pinky nail sized pieces at least.
2. I used Snyder's gluten free pretzel sticks to accomodate my sister and they were very good, they stayed really crunchy.
3. Watch your crust carefully since the edges can burn a bit.
4. Make sure you seal the edges with the cream cheese mixture to keep the jello from leaking down and making your crust soggy.
5.I would prefer more crust so I think you could easily add an extra 25-50% and still have great results, you might need to bake it more though.
6. I added vanilla to my filling for one batch and did not like the results, there was already flavoring enough in the whipped topping. 

If you are wondering what the difference from "Judy's Strawberry Pretzel Salad" is, here you go:
Hers has:
25% less pretzels
150% more sugar in the crust
Double the cream cheese
20% less strawberries
I did not try her recipe so can't judge.

Love this recipe!  the key to success is to make sure to chill well between adding each layer. and as others have said make sure the cream cheese layer goes all the way to the edges so the jello doesn't seep down around it. The first time I made this I used only one 10 oz bag of frozen strawberries instead of two.  I think I like it better that way but that is just personal preference. I also cut the sugar in half in the cream cheese layer and it is still a nicely sweet dessert instead of sickeningly sweet.  again just personal preference!

text:
Strawberry Jello Pretzel salad has been a favorite of my family's since I was a kid growing up, now I get to make it. This is my favorite go to recipe. 

 I don't  measure the pretzels, just enough to cover the bottom so 2+cups. I use a cup of butter. I've found when making this, Refrigerate or even freeze the cream cheese whipped topping onto of the pretzel crust before adding the jello, this really prevents it from leaking down into the pretzel crust and making it soggy. I like to make mine with a few pretzel chunks along with the crumbs.  I also like to add other frozen berries to mine.

Thanks for the recipe! :)

text:
I've made this over the years, but lost the recipe when I moved.  This recipe was just like it and turned out great!  I made sure to buy small pretzels twists (a little thicker than pretzel sticks) and instead of crushing them, I broke them into smaller pieces.  This helped the crust stay crunchy until the dessert was almost all eaten.  In the past, the crust would get soggy almost immediately, ruining it.  This dessert somehow became our Thanksgiving go-to.  It makes it so much easier to find the ingredients in the store at that busy time of year.  No going from store-to-store trying to find pumpkin pie mix, pie shells, etc...Plus it's not as expensive as the pecan pies I make. My family gobbled it up fast!

text:
I read 40 reviews of this dish before I made it.  I opted to add the brown sugar to the crust and only bake for 8 mins.  I made sure to spread the cream cheese all the way to the edges to create a seal.  The top layer, which should be easy, looks awful.  Tip#1 - if you make the jello layer and add frozen, sliced strawberries, DO NOT let sit for an hour before you spread on cream cheese layer - the jello will have gelled. Only let cool for about 15 mins in the fridge before pouring over cream cheese layer.  I am so sad to be taking this ugly dish to my relatives party today.  Tip#2 - always buy extra ingredients.  If I had, I would have remade the jello and tossed the original attempt.

country:

text:
I make this exact receipe all the time and it is a family favorite.  I see how many people comment not to make with low fat cream cheese or sugar free jello because it will not turn out right.  I however, always do and it turns out perfect.  I use neufchatel cheese and after folding in the sugar free whipped topping, I put the mixture in the fridge to set for about 30 minutes while the crust cools.  I put the strawberry jello mixture in the freezer until it gets to a bit firmer than the egg white consistency and then spread the lumpy mixture on top of the cream cheese filling.  Let it set the rest of the way in the fridge for a couple of hours and it all comes together seamlessly!

I have been making this recipe for years.  It is a family favorite.  However, when I make it I put the jello mixture in the pan first as the bottom layer, put it in the refrigerator for several hours or overnight and then spread the cream cheese cool whip mixture on top of the jello.  Sprinkle the pretzels on the top for a crunchy topping.  This guarantees that your jello mixture sets up properly.

text:
Quick and easy. But after a few tries I've made some small changes I feel improve the flavor and presentation.
I use less sugar (1tablespoon) and butter (1/2cup) for the crust, and add a tsp of salt. This increases the salt/sweet ratio for me. 
I also cut the sugar to a 1/2cup for the whip as well. It really doesn't need a whole cup to be really sweet.
Finally, I prefer 1 box of jello, and to slice the strawberries really thin. It has a nice look and evens out the topping to whip flavor in each bite.

This dessert was a huge hit on Christmas Eve. Three (3) cups of fresh strawberries with a about a teaspoon of sugar were used instead of frozen. I froze the diced strawberries in a flat dish. text:
I have been making this for 10+ years and my mom has been making this for me since I was a baby (I am 28 yrs old). I don't change anything except the way I do it. You want to press the pretzels down with parchment paper to make it more compact like crust. The cream cheese I thaw out still in the aluminum packaging in warm/luke warm water so it will mix easily with the whipped cream. Mix the cream cheese with a hand mixer alone first before mixing in the whipped cream. I flash cool the pretzels after being in the oven for 10 min. After I layer the cream mixture on the cooled off pretzels I put it in the fridge overnight or you can put it in the freezer but keep an eye on it. After making the jello you want to make sure it is not anywhere near hot because it could seep through the middle layer and bond to your crust (which makes a really weird texture). I don't usually add any fruit but that's obviously optional :)

text:
What a wonderful dessert salad! I used frozen unsweetened sliced strawberries (wasn't sure if I should use the kind in syrup or au natural, but this worked out well), one of each sugar-free and original strawberry gelatin, and substituted neufchatel (1/3 less fat) cheese for regular cream cheese to lighten it up a bit. This was a big hit at a potluck, though in the future I would make sure to bring it in a dish or container that is designed to stay cool. After sitting out for a while the gelatin got a bit runny and the presentation wasn't as pretty (though this did not affect the flavor). 

In the future I may try to freeze the pretzel crust & cream cheese/cool whip portion first, then add the gelatin and strawberries an hour or two before serving. I think the frozen middle will help it to stay pretty longer and add another texture. If it's a hot day, I may also place my 9x13 pay into a larger pan filled with ice to keep it cool & pretty.

Do make sure that the whipped topping cream cheese mixture  completely covers all the pretzel crust. If there are any gaps the gelatin will leak down into the pretzel crust and make it soggy.

The combination of sweet/creamy/salty is sure to please the palate. It's one of those dishes that even people who normally don't like jello will enjoy & go back for seconds!

text:
Fantastic dessert! Here are a few tips I've learned while making it:
1-Chop the frozen strawberries to bite size before putting in jello.
2-Spread the white filling all the way to the edges of the pan so the jello does not ooze down to the pretzel layer.
3-works really well with frozen rasperries and raspberry jello too. In fact, I prefer the raspberries because it gives a nice tart taste to the sweet and salty.

text:
I do like this recipe so far, although it is still chilling in my fridge. I have not tasted the finished result yet. I  am bringing this to a Church potluck tomorrow. I wish the recipe was more specific about the pretzels. I measured 2 cups of pretzels and then crushed them in a ziplock bag. I wish that I would have known that I needed to measure 2 cups of crushed pretzels. I also recommend applying the cream cheese layer very gently, so the pretzel crust does not accidentally get "pulled" into the cream cheese/whipped cream. I will update my review tomorrow, after the potluck!!
   Update, everyone at my church potluck was raving about this!! It was a huge success, and I am changing my rating to 5 stars. This is a fun dessert to make with the perfect combination of salty and sweet. I love that this is not a heavy dessert!! It truly was delicious. This will be brought to many potlucks again in the future. Very happy with the finished result.

Osowoofy

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I made this yesterday, and it's even better the next day!
The pretzel crust and the cream cheese layer I made almost exactly as the recipe states -- the only difference is that I doubled the cream cheese layer because my baking dish was a bit taller.  I used mini pretzels that didn't seem to be quite as salty as regular-sized pretzels, so I felt like I didn't get quite the contrast between sweet and salty as when I've tried this dish in the past.  Really, the Jell-O layer is where you can put your own spin on this: I used a bag of frozen strawberries (thawed) and a can of crushed pineapple and I boiled the strawberry liquid along with the liquid from crushed pineapple to go in the gelatin. Also used one strawberry and one cherry Jell-O, which really gave it more of a "tart/sweet" flavor.  In the end, i'm glad I doubled the cream cheese layer, because the gelatin layer ended up being intensely concentrated, and I believe the larger cream cheese layer balanced that fruity flavor nicely.  I also pureed half of the strawberries to give a better overall texture, and placed the fruit in a bowl in the freezer to help it "gel" the gelatin quicker.   
I might be in the minority here, but in the past I've had this with the pretzel layer "soggy," and didn't really mind it. But again, that's a personal observation.

text:
Read other cooks reviews before making this recipe. Loved the taste, which was much different than expected - great idea mixing salt and sweet together. Instead of using white sugar, I substituted it with Altern (WalMart-brand) sugar. Rather than use frozen strawberries, I sliced fresh ones. Was disappointed that the pretzels did not form a crust during cooling process - it looked great in the glass dish before it went into the frig. I may use more butter next time. Pretzel crust was more like powder - a friend solved that. He turned the pretzel crust upside down instead of putting it on the dish. The pretzel powder covered the rest of the dessert; great taste, he said. After making the second time, I will come back and give another review.
